ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-item {
    counter-increment: list-counter-alpha;
}

ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-marker::before {
    content: counter(list-counter-alpha, lower-alpha);
}

/* Level 3: Lowercase roman numerals */

    counter-reset: list-counter-roman;
}

    counter-increment: list-counter-roman;
}

ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-marker::before {
    content: counter(list-counter-roman, lower-roman);
}

data-stale="false" width="auto"><div class="stMarkdown" data-testid="stMarkdown"><div data-testid="stMarkdownContainer" class="st-emotion-cache-1104ytp e1icttdg0"><p><strong>Processing file:</strong> Unit_1_Professionalism_and_Trends.pdf</p></div></div></div><div class="stElementContainer element-container st-emotion-cache-kj6hex eu6p4el1" data-testid="stElementContainer" data-stale="false" width="auto"><div class="stMarkdown" data-testid="stMarkdown"><div data-testid="stMarkdownContainer" class="st-emotion-cache-1104ytp e1icttdg0"><p>UNIT ONE: PROFESSIONALISM AND TRENDS IN NURSING</p>
<p>In this unit you will cover nursing as a profession, characteristics of a professional nurse, professional organisations, the Nursing Council of Kenya and the legal aspects of nursing in Kenya. You will also cover disciplines of nursing and professional practice and conclude with a study of trends in nursing practice and the nursing process. It will build on what you have already learnt and it will also serve as revision.</p>
<p>This unit is composed of two sections:
Section One: Professionalism and Trends in Nursing.
Section Two: The Nursing Process.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-one-professionalism-and-trends-in-nursing">SECTION ONE: PROFESSIONALISM AND TRENDS IN NURSING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-one-professionalism-and-trends-in-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="unit-objectives">Unit Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this unit you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Perform professional duties in conformity with the ICN code of ethics</li>
<li>Demonstrate an understanding of the legal aspects of nursing practice in Kenya</li>
<li>Display the characteristics of a professional nurse</li>
<li>Apply the nursing process to provide quality care</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Welcome to section one of this unit on professionalism and trends in nursing that directly relates to clinical practice.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe trends in nursing</li>
<li>Describe professionalism</li>
<li>List the national, regional and international professional organisations and their relationships</li>
<li>Describe the Nursing Council of Kenya</li>
<li>List the legal aspects of nursing in Kenya</li>
<li>Describe the disciplines of nursing in Kenya</li>
<li>Describe professional practice</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="profession">Profession<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#profession" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>You are already working in the nursing profession, and now you are being trained to become a Kenya Registered Community Health Nurse. On completion of this</p>
<p>programme, you will be expected to be proficient in providing general nursing, reproductive health and community health services.</p>
<p>This section of unit one, aims at moulding you to become a professional nurse. You will at all times, whether on or off duty, be expected to display certain professional characteristics. You will begin by defining a profession, a professional nurse and professional nursing practice.</p>
<p>Bailliere's Nurses dictionary defines a profession as a 'calling, vocation requiring specialised knowledge, methods and skills, as well as preparation in an institution of higher learning in the scholarly, scientific and historical principles underlying such methods and skills'. The dictionary further states that members of a profession are committed to continuing study, to enlarging their body of knowledge, to placing service above personal gain and to providing practical services, vital to human society and social welfare. It adds that a profession functions autonomously and is committed to higher standards of achievement and conduct (Baillieres').</p>
<p>You may be familiar with reputable professions such as engineering, law and medicine. All these professions have similar characteristics.</p>
<p>The nursing profession is distinguished by its philosophy of care, full time commitment to human well being, particular blend of knowledge and skills, valuable service to the community and the regulation of its practice.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-are-the-characteristics-of-a-profession">What are the characteristics of a profession?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-the-characteristics-of-a-profession" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Make a note of some of your thoughts on a notepad and then click the link below to check your answer.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="did-you-think-of-the-following">Did you think of the following?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#did-you-think-of-the-following" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>A profession:</p>
<ul>
<li>Has a theoretical body of knowledge and skills</li>
<li>Encourages full time commitment to service, establishing standards of practice which are maintained by all members</li>
<li>Exercises self-discipline</li>
<li>Protects the public</li>
<li>Is responsible for the advancement of the profession</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 3 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Develops its ethics to accommodate new demands and circumstances of the profession</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="professional-nurse">Professional Nurse<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#professional-nurse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A professional nurse is an individual who has successfully undergone a prescribed nursing training programme, has passed a licensing examination and is registered by the national nursing regulatory body, in our context the Nursing Council of Kenya (NCK).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-of-a-professional-nurse">Characteristics of a Professional Nurse<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-a-professional-nurse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A professional nurse:</p>
<ul>
<li>Displays high standards of performance and integrity in nursing practice</li>
<li>Seeks constantly to improve her/his technical and interpersonal skills through continuing education and research</li>
<li>Uses sound judgement and discretion in dealing with patients/clients and their relatives</li>
<li>Provides holistic care to patients, family and community</li>
<li>Deals competently with crisis situations</li>
<li>Puts what is good for professional services to patients ahead of self-interest</li>
<li>Coordinates and evaluates nursing services in cooperation with members of other health services (collaboration and networking)</li>
<li>Is not overly concerned with the materialistic aspects of nursing</li>
<li>Expects to find satisfaction and spiritual values in their work</li>
<li>Feels responsible for the status of nursing and tries to advance and never to retard it</li>
<li>Has inner resources to which she/he can turn to, for renewal of faith and courage when weary and discouraged</li>
<li>Is proud of her/his profession and considers it to be at par with other professions like medicine or law or any other vocation practised for compensation, which at the same time contributes in its own unique way to the welfare of humanity</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="personal-attributes">Personal Attributes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personal-attributes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Personal attributes that help a nurse to display professionalism include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Good personal appearance with a voice that does not scare patients</li>
<li>A ready smile, gentle hand, orderly in thought and action</li>
<li>Emotionally mature, compassionate, dignified, tolerant, friendly, sympathetic and interested in other people</li>
</ul>
<p>All characteristics are advantageous to the creation of a friendly and conducive environment for the patient's recovery. As a nurse, you must at all times have serenity of mind and self-control to be able to handle a variety of situations and patients.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong> A professional nurse at all times displays integrity, commitment and ethical behaviour. They display intelligence, good judgement and handle emergencies well.</p>
<p>A professional nurse is also responsible in professional and social situations.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="personal-grooming">Personal Grooming<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personal-grooming" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Personal grooming is very important to nurses. Remember, every patient has a mental picture or image of how their nurse should be. The nurse's appearance provides security and hope to a patient.</p>
<p>A nurse's uniform should not be tight or very loose to hinder free movement during an emergency. It must be very clean to prevent cross infection and is to be well pressed. The dress or skirt should be below the knee cap to give allowance for bending. The material should not be 'see-through'.</p>
<p>Female nurses should avoid bright inner wear especially if their uniform is white. The uniform should be well maintained, that is, fallen buttons or torn zippers should be replaced, rips and tears mended and stains removed.</p>
<p>As you are aware, hair is a source of microorganisms. Female nurses should tie back long hair neatly. Male nurses should have their beards and moustaches neatly shaven. The nurse's cap should be worn neatly and securely.</p>
<p>Shoes should be low-heeled and soft to avoid making excessive noise, which may disturb patients. The nurse should maintain daily care of shoes, socks or stockings in order to prevent cross infection. Nails should be trimmed and coloured nail polish avoided. The freedom to wear jewellery, watches, pens, scissors or handkerchiefs will depend on individual hospital regulations</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong> The patients have a right to identify the nurse who is providing their care. It is advisable therefore to wear an identification tag at all times showing full names and qualifications.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-ethics">Nursing Ethics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-ethics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You are being prepared to practise professional nursing which involves adherence to the code of ethics.</p>
<p>Collin's dictionary defines ethics as:</p>
<ul>
<li>Moral principles</li>
<li>Code of behaviour</li>
<li>Study of morals</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>We can further define ethics as morals and philosophical principles that define actions as being either right or wrong. The ethical concepts touch on your practice as you interact with other people, the society, co-workers and the profession.</p>
<p><strong>Remember</strong>: The patient is to be at the centre of your practice. Patients have the right to contribute to their own care and as you provide care, always remember to respect the beliefs, values and customs of the patient.</p>
<p>As a professional nurse you are expected to uphold and abide by the code of ethics.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="guidelines">Guidelines<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#guidelines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>You should always hold personal information in confidence and use your discretion in sharing this information.</li>
<li>You should always remember that it is your responsibility to keep abreast with current trends in the nursing profession so as to maintain competence in nursing practice through continuing education.</li>
<li>Always maintain the highest standards of nursing care possible within the given reality of a specific situation.</li>
<li>When accepting any responsibilities delegated to you, ensure that you are competent to carry out the assignment.</li>
<li>Maintain professional standards of personal conduct that reflect credit upon the profession at all times.</li>
<li>Share with other citizens the responsibility for initiating and supporting action to meet the health and social needs of the public during your practice.</li>
<li>Sustain a co-operating relationship with co-workers in nursing and other fields.</li>
<li>Take appropriate action to safeguard the individual when a co-worker or any other person endangers their care.</li>
<li>You have a major role in determining and implementing desirable standards of nursing practice and nursing education.</li>
<li>Be active in developing a core of professional knowledge.</li>
<li>Acting through a professional organisation, you are to participate in establishing and maintaining equitable social and economic working conditions in nursing. This, therefore, means that you are to be a member of your professional association.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="have-you-heard-of-the-international-council-of-nurses-code-of-ethics">Have you heard of the International Council of Nurses Code of Ethics?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#have-you-heard-of-the-international-council-of-nurses-code-of-ethics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The International Council of Nurses (ICN) Code of Ethics was adopted in Mexico City in 1973. It states that the fundamental responsibility of the nurse is to promote health, prevent illness, restore health and alleviate suffering. Moreover, the need for nursing is universal. Inherent in nursing is respect for life, dignity and the rights of man.</p>
<p>Nurses are to provide care to individuals regardless of nationality, race, creed, colour, age, sex, politics or social status. As a nurse you will be providing health care to the individual, family and the community. You will be operating in teams, such as a nursing team which is within a health team.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="code-of-ethics-international-council-of-nurses">CODE OF ETHICS (INTERNATIONAL COUNCIL OF NURSES)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#code-of-ethics-international-council-of-nurses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ethical-concepts-applied-to-nursing">Ethical Concepts Applied to Nursing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ethical-concepts-applied-to-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The fundamental responsibility of the nurse is fourfold; to promote health, to prevent illness, to restore health and to alleviate suffering.</p>
<p>The need for nursing is universal. Inherent in nursing is respect for life, dignity and rights of man. It is unrestricted by considerations of nationality, race, creed, colour, age, sex, politics or social status.</p>
<p>Nurses render health services to the individual, the family and the community and coordinate their services with those of related groups.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nurses-and-people">Nurses and people<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nurses-and-people" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The nurse's primary responsibility is to those people who require nursing care.</p>
<p>The nurse, in providing care, promotes an environment in which the values, customs and spiritual beliefs of the individual are respected.</p>
<p>The nurse holds in confidence personal information and uses judgement in sharing this information.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nurses-and-practice">Nurses and practice<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nurses-and-practice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The nurse carries personal responsibility for nurse practice and for maintaining competence by continual learning.</p>
<p>The nurse maintains the highest standards of nursing care possible within the reality of a specific situation.</p>
<p>The nurse uses judgement in relation to individual competence when accepting and delegating responsibilities.</p>
<p>The nurse when acting in professional capacity should at all times maintain standards of personal conduct which reflect credit upon the profession.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 5 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 6 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nurse-and-co-workers">Nurse and Co-workers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nurse-and-co-workers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The nurse sustains a cooperative relationship with co-workers in nursing and other fields.</p>
<p>The nurse takes appropriate action to safeguard the individual when their care is endangered by a co-worker or any other person.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nurses-and-the-profession">Nurses and the profession<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nurses-and-the-profession" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The nurse plays the major role in determining and implementing desirable standards of nursing practice and nursing education.</p>
<p>The nurse is active in developing a core of professional knowledge.</p>
<p>The nurse, acting through the professional organisation, participates in establishing and maintaining equitable social and economic working conditions in nursing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="code-of-ethics-as-applied-to-nursing">Code of Ethics as applied to Nursing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#code-of-ethics-as-applied-to-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Nurses minister to the sick, assume responsibility for creating a physical, social and spiritual environment which will be conducive to recovery and stress the prevention of illness and promotion of health by teaching and example. They render health service to the individual, the family and the community and co-ordinate their services with members of other health professions.</p>
<p>Service to mankind is the primary function of nurses and the reason for the existence of the nursing profession. The need for a nursing service is universal. Professional nursing service is based on human need and is therefore unrestricted by considerations of nationality, race, creed, colour, politics or social status.</p>
<p>Inherent in the code is the fundamental concept that the nurse believes in the essential freedoms of mankind and in the preservation of human life. It is important that all nurses be aware of the Red Cross Principles and of their rights and obligations.</p>
<p>The profession recognises that an international code cannot cover in detail all the activities and relationships of nurses, some of which are conditioned by personal philosophies and beliefs.</p>
<ol>
<li>The fundamental responsibility of the nurse is threefold; to conserve life, to alleviate suffering and to promote health.</li>
<li>The nurse shall maintain at all times the highest standards of nursing care and of professional conduct.</li>
<li>The nurse must not only be well prepared to practice but shall maintain knowledge and skill at a consistently high level.</li>
<li>The religious beliefs of a patient shall be respected.</li>
<li>Nurses hold in confidence all personal information entrusted to them.</li>
<li>Nurses recognise not only the responsibilities but the limitations of their professional functions, do not recommend or give medical treatment without medical orders except in emergencies, and report such action to a physician as soon as possible.</li>
<li>The nurse is under an obligation to carry out the physician's orders intelligently and loyally and to refuse to participate in unethical procedures.</li>
<li>The nurse sustains confidence in the physician and other members of the health team; incompetence or unethical conduct of associates should be exposed but only to the proper authority.</li>
<li>The nurse is entitled to just remuneration and accepts only such compensation as the contract, actual or implied, provides.</li>
<li>Nurses do not permit their names to be used in connection with the advertisement of products or with any other forms of self advertisement.</li>
<li>The nurse co-operates with and maintains harmonious relationships with members of other professions and with nursing colleagues.</li>
<li>The nurse adheres to standards of personal ethics which reflect credit upon the profession.</li>
<li>In personal conduct, nurses should not knowingly disregard the accepted pattern of behaviour of the community in which they live and work.</li>
<li>The nurse participates and shares responsibilities with other citizens and other health professions in promoting efforts to meet the health needs of the public  local, state, national and international.</li>
</ol>
<p>The professional nurse also has to be knowledgeable of what they are practising at the health facility and should acquire the technical skills that will assist in and improve the work performance.</p>
<p>You may be asking yourself, "How does the Code of Nurses affect me during my daily practice?"</p>
<p>The 'Code' incorporates general statements of principle applicable to all circumstances, upon infringement of which a nurse practitioner is liable to disciplinary action or penalty or both.</p>
<p>The Code of Ethics embodies the standards by which each nurse practitioner forms a conscience, a capacity for moral reasoning and governs the practice of nursing.</p>
<p>You should also get yourself a copy of the Procedure Manual from the Nursing Council of Kenya, (at a fee) if you do not have one. It will assist you both in your daily work and in the study of this course.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="professional-organisations">Professional Organisations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#professional-organisations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Now we are going to discuss some professional nursing organisations which include:</p>
<ul>
<li>National Nurses Association of Kenya (NNAK)</li>
<li>East Central Southern Africa College of Nursing (ECSACON)</li>
<li>International Council of Nurses (ICN)</li>
</ul>
<p>Nurses in Kenya, just like any other countries in the world, are members of professional organisations at national, regional and global levels.</p>
<p>In Kenya the professional nursing organisation that has both regional and international recognition is the National Nurses Association of Kenya (NNAK).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-national-nurses-association-of-kenya">The National Nurses Association of Kenya<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-national-nurses-association-of-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The National Nurses Association of Kenya (NNAK) is a professional association for nurses, which is registered by the Registrar of Societies as a welfare association.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="membership">Membership<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#membership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Membership of NNAK is open to all nurses who are either registered or enrolled by the Nursing Council of Kenya. Student nurses can join as associate members.</p>
<p>There are two types of membership:</p>
<ul>
<li>Life membership</li>
<li>Ordinary membership</li>
</ul>
<p>The Association has branches in all provinces. Members in each branch elect a Branch Chairman, Secretary and Treasurer. In turn, these elect national office bearers every two years who comprise the National Chairman, Vice Chairman, Secretary, Treasurer, Organising Secretary and their respective Vices.</p>
<p>The Association has an Executive Committee which comprises of national office bearers and branch chairmen. Various nursing disciplines are represented as chapters, for example,</p>
<p>midwives, operating theatre nurses, mental health and psychiatric nurses, educationists, intensive care nurses and private practice nurses. The headquarters of NNAK is in Nairobi.</p>
<p>NNAK is a member of a regional body known as the East Central Southern Africa College of Nursing (ECSACON) whose offices are situated in Arusha, Tanzania, the Association of Professional Societies of East Africa (APSEA) and the International Council of Nurses (ICN) situated in Geneva.</p>
<p>Additionally, NNAK collaborates with other professional bodies such as the Royal College of Nurses, Royal College of Midwives, the Canadian Nurses Association, American Nurses Association, Kenya Medical Association (KMA), the Association of Kenya Obstetricians/Gynaecologists (KOGS) and other health organisations.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="functions-of-the-national-nurses-association-of-kenya">Functions of the National Nurses Association of Kenya<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-the-national-nurses-association-of-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The functions of the National Nurses Association of Kenya are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Promoting nursing and maintaining the honour, interest and practice of all aspects of the profession as a whole</li>
<li>Promoting and maintaining high standards of nursing education</li>
<li>Stimulating and encouraging nursing research</li>
<li>Promoting co-operation between this body and other national and international professional bodies</li>
<li>Promoting good understanding between the Association, central and local governments and all communities</li>
<li>Acting as a local representative body of the nursing profession</li>
<li>Supporting a high standard of nursing ethics, conduct and practice which is organised and functions unrestricted by consideration of nationality, race, creed, politics, sex or social status</li>
<li>Assisting whenever possible members who by reason of adversity or ill health are in need of help</li>
<li>Arranging and holding periodic meetings of the Association for professional, educational and social purposes</li>
<li>Circulating such information as may be thought necessary by means of a journal, bulletin or any other method</li>
<li>Accepting or refusing any gift endowed or bequest made to or acquired by the Association or for the purposes of any specific object connected with the science, art of nursing and executing any charitable</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>or other trusts which may be considered expedient or desirable in the interests of the Association</p>
<ul>
<li>Maintaining an up to date list of all members in Section 4 a (i), (ii) and (iv) of the NNAK constitution</li>
<li>Performing all such other lawful things as may from time to time be conducive to the attainment of furtherance of the above functions. (NNAK Constitution, section 3 1987)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chapters">Chapters<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chapters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The chapters of NNAK include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Midwives</li>
<li>Education</li>
<li>Theatre Nurses</li>
<li>Mental Health and Psychiatric Nurses</li>
<li>General Nurses</li>
<li>Private Nurse Practitioners</li>
<li>Paediatric Nurses</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="national-executive-committee">National Executive Committee<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#national-executive-committee" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a very large committee comprising the national executives who run the office at the headquarters (the National Chairman, two Vice Chairmen, an Honorary Secretary and the Vice Treasurer, Organising Secretary and the Editor).</p>
<p>Other members are the Branch Chairmen, Chairmen of Chapters, Division of Nursing (MOH) and the Nursing Council of Kenya. Other committees in the NNAK are the Education, Editorial and Finance Committees.</p>
<p>The Division of Nursing, on behalf of the Ministry of Health, deals with employment issues for nurses and sponsorship for higher education. Furthermore, it provides working facilities for nurses, technical know how and supervision. On the other hand, the Nursing Council of Kenya deals with training of nurses, maintenance of standards of nursing education and nursing practice and, additionally, the regulation of nurses' conduct. Finally, NNAK serves as an advocate for the nurses and the community.</p>
<p>The NNAK's activities, as you will note, are geared towards promoting excellence in nursing. There are national activities such as the Florence Nightingale week, Annual General Meetings, branch activities and chapter activities which aim to improve the quality of nursing and reproductive health care. Finally, there are those activities channelled by ICN/ECSACON through the Ministry of Health. Apart from the discussed activities, there are several meetings conducted at the NNAK, such as quarterly Executive Committee meetings and monthly meetings for the chapters.</p>
<p>The following are just some brief highlights of what you will acquire from the NNAK:</p>
<ul>
<li>Updates in knowledge, attitude and skills in nursing and midwifery practice to improve your performance for quality care to patients/clients</li>
<li>Interactions and the opportunity to share experiences with other nurses</li>
<li>The formation of links with other organisations</li>
<li>Advocacy on welfare issues such as better education as well as better remuneration and improved conditions of service</li>
</ul>
<p>So far we have been discussing your professional body, which is a member of a regional body known as ECSACON. Let us now highlight a few points about this body.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-east-central-southern-africa-college-of-nursing-ecsacon">The East Central Southern Africa College of Nursing (ECSACON)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-east-central-southern-africa-college-of-nursing-ecsacon" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>ECSACON is a professional agency of the Commonwealth Regional Health Community (CRHC). Its main objective is to promote and reinforce professional excellence through the development of programmes. It is expected that this will, in turn, strengthen nursing and midwifery practice, education, research, leadership and management to improve service delivery and uplift the quality of health of the communities in the East Central Southern Africa (ECSA) region.</p>
<p>ECSACON is a corporate body of nurses and midwives of member states comprising Botswana, Lesotho, Kenya, Malawi, Mauritius, Mozambique, Namibia, Seychelles, South Africa, Swaziland, Tanzania, Uganda, Zambia, Zimbabwe and any other states that will accede to membership of CRHC for the ECSA region.</p>
<p>The membership of the college consists of individual nurses/midwifes and Professional organisations such as:</p>
<ul>
<li>National Nurse/Midwifery Association (NNAS/NMAS)</li>
<li>National Nursing Councils (NNCS)</li>
</ul>
<p>An individual can become a member once registered by the Nurses Regulatory Body as a nurse/midwife in any of the member states.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="benefits-of-membership-to-ecsacon">Benefits of Membership to ECSACON<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#benefits-of-membership-to-ecsacon" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The first benefit is knowledge. This knowledge is obtained through the many activities ECSACON conducts, such as quadrennial conferences where nurses from member countries meet and share research finding on</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>topics of national interests in health. They exchange information on various topical issues on nursing, midwifery and health, mapping the way forward for excellence in nursing/midwifery, education and practice.</p>
<p>Interacting with nurses from the region is a benefit on its own. Apart from this, ECSACON has conducted many projects, for example, on research, leadership and management, advocacy and so on.</p>
<p>Members are also provided with reading materials through the CNR or Nursing Council.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="members-also-have-rights-and-privileges-ecsacon-membership-rights-and-privileges">Members also have rights and privileges . ECSACON - Membership Rights and Privileges<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#members-also-have-rights-and-privileges-ecsacon-membership-rights-and-privileges" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The membership rights and privileges of ECSACON are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Voting and speaking at the ECSACON meetings</li>
<li>Nominating candidates for ECSACON elections and Standing Committees</li>
<li>Participating in ECSACON conferences, workshops, seminars and other professional activities as appropriately promoted by ECSACON</li>
<li>Nominating candidates for ECSACON fellowships and awards</li>
<li>Receiving professional guidance and assistance from ECSACON</li>
<li>Receiving from or through ECSACON documents and periodic information about activities and news about nursing worldwide</li>
<li>Having their professional articles of regional and international interest published in ECSACON newsletter/journal/magazines</li>
<li>Enjoying benefits established by ECSACON</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="international-council-of-nurses-icn">International Council of Nurses (ICN)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#international-council-of-nurses-icn" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The International Council of Nurses is a federation of nurses' associations (NNAS) in 122 countries. It was founded in 1899. ICN was the first health professionals' organisations to be formed and remains the largest among international organisations relating to the provision of health care. It is operated by nurses for nurses.</p>
<p>The Secretariat of the ICN is based in Geneva and consists of a president, a chief executive and members. ICN works to ensure quality nursing and sound health policies for all. It strives for the advancement of nursing knowledge and the presence of a worldwide</p>
<p>respected nursing profession and a competent, satisfied nursing workforce.</p>
<p>The ICN has goals and core values that guide its activities..</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="goals">Goals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#goals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The goals of ICN are to influence health and nursing globally and strengthen national nurses associations.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="values">Values<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#values" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The values of ICN are to encourage visionary leadership, inclusiveness, flexibility and partnership among all member states and the achievement of excellence in nursing/midwifery education and practice.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vision">Vision<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vision" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The ICN states that its vision is to unite all nurses within the ICN to speak with one voice as advocates of all that ICN serves; to acknowledge that a human being has the right to preventive and curative care; to spearhead the health care progress and shape health policy around the world through enhancing nurses' expertise, strength, their numbers, alignment of their efforts and collaboration with the public and other health professionals. The ICN mission statement is derived from this vision.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mission">Mission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The ICN's mission is to lead societies to better health and to promote healthy lifestyles, workplaces and communities; to support strategies which alleviate poverty, pollution and other causes of illness, while incorporating science and advanced technology in the provision of compassionate and ethical caring; to shape nursing education in accordance with values, policies, standards and conditions that free nurses to practise to the full extent of their education and abilities within multi-disciplinary health teams.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="philosophy">Philosophy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#philosophy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The ICN philosophy entails commitment to caring, advocating on behalf of patients, and helping people help themselves. ICN ensures that the nursing profession is highly valued, appropriately utilised, recognised, rewarded and represented throughout the healthcare system.</p>
<p>You have now gone through the ICN vision, mission and philosophy. You should have identified some crucial themes such as the role of the nurse as:</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Provider of nursing care and health services</li>
<li>Policy maker</li>
<li>Collaborator with the public and other health professionals</li>
</ul>
<p>Health is a universal right of every human being regardless of the social status. You have to encompass teamwork within multidisciplinary teams.</p>
<p>Finally, you have to keep abreast by incorporating science and technology into the health delivery services in nursing practice. You will now study trends in nursing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="historical-background">Historical Background<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#historical-background" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Historically the nursing practice in Kenya, just like anywhere else in the world, was performed on a tradition that sick people received care from female family members in their own homes. Therefore, it can be said that the family is the oldest and the most used health care delivery service in the world. Currently this approach to care provision is known as 'family nursing'.</p>
<p>Florence Nightingale (1869) stated: "...it has been said and written scores of times that every woman makes a good nurse, but I believe, on the contrary, that the elements of nursing are all but unknown...". She further stated: "It is well known that nursing exists to serve the society."</p>
<p>As social conditions and health care needs change, the nurses' roles and nursing practices continue to alter in response to these changes. Florence Nightingale is the founder of professional nursing. She initiated formal nursing training using a curriculum replacing apprenticeship.</p>
<p>Western medicine in Kenya was introduced with the arrival of missionaries in 1895. Doctors and nurses were brought from Britain and Europe. They trained dressers and assistants on the job. Later on they began to conduct basic training in missionary hospitals. In 1949, a nurses, midwives and health visitors council was formed by an ordinance. In 1950, formal nursing training at enrolled and registered levels was started. The practice of nursing followed a medical model. The patient was nursed as fragments of diseased body parts using task allocation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="task-allocation-job-assignment">Task Allocation/Job Assignment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#task-allocation-job-assignment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This method of dividing duties was based on the industrial concept of division of labour. The patient was fragmented into a series of jobs assigned to different nurses of different grades. Thus a hierarchy of tasks and staff was created for patients. This resulted in a</p>
<p>fragmentation and lack of continuity of care, with patients subordinated to the system rather than being central to it.</p>
<p>You may recall a practice in the wards whereby the most junior nurse was assigned sluice rooms, others observations, wound dressings, drug administration, specimen collection, theatre cases, doctors round and so on.</p>
<p>In the 1950s, nurse leaders in North America began to recognise that the development of nursing knowledge and practice must run simultaneously with research. Florence Nightingale in 1859 wrote that nursing was more than the administration of medicine and application of poultices. This shows that Florence Nightingale had recognised that nursing needed a combination of both intellectual and practical skills.</p>
<p>In the 1960s to 1980s, many developments and changes in nursing took place stemming from the professional desire for innovation and change in practice. The nurses' leaders felt that the patient was alienated from their own care, and that there was a need for improvements in nursing. Nurse leaders began trying to demonstrate that nursing was a profession with its own unique body of knowledge.</p>
<p>Virginia Henderson (1966) delineates the unique functions of the nurse as follows:</p>
<p>"...to assist the individual, sick or well, in the performance of those activities contributing to health or its recovery (or to peaceful death) that he would perform unaided if he had the necessary strength, will, knowledge. And to do this in such a way as to help him gain independence as rapidly as possible."</p>
<p>In the search for a unique body of knowledge, nurse theorists were using scientific methods to describe, explain and predict nursing practice and its outcomes. You must be wondering how these developments were reflected on nursing in Kenya?</p>
<p>In the 1960s and 1970s task allocation was exclusively practised in the context of hospital nursing. Task assignment is still practised when there is shortage of staff. During the said period, however, lots of changes took place in the health delivery system in Kenya.</p>
<p>Politically, independence was attained in 1963. The KANU manifesto declared its intention to fight what it saw as the three greatest enemies of development: poverty, illiteracy and disease. Within this context, health care had to be made available to the community. This led to the</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>introduction of community health nursing training (KECHN) in 1966 at MTC Kisumu.</p>
<p>Midwifery training had already been introduced in the 1950's at enrolled level, and at registered level in 1965. At the same time, expatriate nurses who were administrators of nursing services, and nursing educators were leaving the country at independence. In anticipation of gaps in training and skills, a Diploma in Advanced Nursing was started in 1968 at the University of Nairobi to prepare Nurse Educators and administrators.</p>
<p>The shift to community health nursing was to provide preventive and promotive health care service delivery.</p>
<p>Florence Nightingale (1867), states in her private notes, "my vision ...is that the ultimate destination of all nursing is the care of the sick in their own homes ...I look to the abolition of all hospitals and workhouse infirmaries. But it is no use to talk about the year 2000."</p>
<p>Do you think this was a prediction of the global Primary Health Care Concept of 'Health for all by the year 2000'?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-is-health">What is Health?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Many people think that health is the absence of illness but the World Health Organisation (WHO) in 1946 defined health as a state of complete physical, mental and social wellbeing and not merely the absence of disease or infirmity. The health delivery services in the 1970's laid great emphasis on community-based health care in the implementation of Primary Health care concept (WHO, 1978).</p>
<p>Nurse leaders worldwide became dissatisfied with the task allocation method of organising patient care as it alienated the patient from the nursing care.</p>
<p>Nurses felt that there should be accountability of the care being given with a view to improving the quality of care.</p>
<p>Therefore, in the 1980's nurses started moving away from 'tasks' to individualised nursing care. This move away from a pre-occupation with tasks to a focus on patients led to the introduction of a nursing process that provided a systematic method for individualised nursing.</p>
<p>The progression of these systems started with patient allocation to team nursing and then primary nursing</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-nursing-process">The Nursing Process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-nursing-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The nursing process was introduced in the 1970s in North America and 1980s in Britain. In 1977, the United Kingdom Central Council (UKCC) recognised the nursing process and decreed that the care of patients should be studied and practised in the sequence of the nursing process. (Dickinson,1982).</p>
<p>The British nurses viewed this type of introduction with suspicion, since it was done in haste, adopting a top-down approach and coercive change strategy that led to misunderstandings and difficulties. The same trend was visible in Kenya in the late 1970s, bringing confusion to the nurses in the clinical practices who, up to now, assumed that the nursing process is an assessment tool for nursing students and not a guideline for patient care</p>
<p>The argument most nurses present is that good nurses have always used the nursing process even though they did not analyse what they were doing in terms of a process or steps and did not document the information in an orderly and comprehensive manner.</p>
<p>Thus, the nursing process is wholly feasible in the context of practice, which is organised on the basis of patient allocation, team nursing or primary nursing. Assessing, planning, implementing and evaluating are embedded in everyday nursing practice.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="patient-centred-systems-of-organising-nursing-care">Patient Centred Systems of Organising Nursing Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#patient-centred-systems-of-organising-nursing-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="patient-allocation">Patient Allocation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#patient-allocation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Each nurse is allocated a small number of patients (up to six) to look after during a whole work shift.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-dae79fe8.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="team-nursing">Team Nursing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#team-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>As you probably know, the nursing staff in a ward is divided into teams, each team taking responsibility for the total care of a subgroup of the patients.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-bc4b1fd4.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="primary-nursing">Primary Nursing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is a patient-centred nursing system. One nurse</p>
<p>(the primary nurse) assumes individual responsibility for a particular patient. Theoretically this responsibility extends over the entire period the patient requires nursing although in practice there has to be delegation to other nurses (the associate nurses) during periods of absence from the ward. The potential benefits of primary nursing for patients are continuity of care and cover.</p>
<p>The concept of primary nursing responds to the directive of putting patients first and it embodies the ideals of individualised nursing. Therefore, if nurses are to accomplish the goals of nursing as defined by the nursing leader, nursing must have a body of theoretical knowledge on which to base its practice. This will be achieved through conducting nursing researches at the clinical sites.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-27f18fd2.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-models">Nursing Models<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-models" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A nursing model as defined by Riehl &amp; Roy (1980) is a systematically constructed, scientifically based and logically related set of concepts of nursing practice together with the theoretical bases of these concepts and the values required for their use by the practitioner. Models are developed carefully and methodically, usually as a result of prolonged research and may involve many months or years of observing nursing practice and thinking about why nursing is carried out.</p>
<p>Fawcett (1984) quoted Reilly (1975) who said: "We all have a private image (concept) of nursing practice. In turn this private image influences our interpretations of data, our decisions and our actions. But can a discipline continue to develop when its members hold so many differing private images? The proponents of conceptual models of practice are seeking to make us aware of private images so that we can begin to identify commodities in our perception of the nature of practice..."</p>
<p>Conceptual models for nursing are, therefore, the formal presentation of private images of nursing. They consist of many concepts, which identify the essential components of the disciplines. They show relationships between the concepts and may introduce already established theories from other disciplines, which are applicable for nursing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-values-of-nursing-models">The Values of Nursing Models<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-values-of-nursing-models" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A model can be useful for nursing practice, education, management and research. In nursing practice, a model provides a framework for what a nurse does and how they do it.</p>
<p>In nursing education, a model provides a framework, which organises the curriculum, the knowledge, skills and approaches, which are necessary for learning and practice.</p>
<p>In management, a model can outline the common goals to be achieved. In research, a model provides guidance about what should be studied in order to extend nursing knowledge and thus improve knowledge.</p>
<p>Various models have already been developed. They include Orem's self-care model (Orem 1971), which model depicts nursing as assisting individuals to their optimal level of self-care.</p>
<p>Roy (1970) centred her model on the concept of adaptation. Rogers (1970) focused on the concept of environment and the nursing of a client (patient) interacting with the environment.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 12 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>The various models have the following in common:</p>
<ul>
<li>Person</li>
<li>Health</li>
<li>Nursing activities/process</li>
<li>Environment</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="theories-of-nursing">Theories of Nursing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#theories-of-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-is-a-theory">What is a Theory?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-a-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>A theory is a generalised explanation of a phenomenon. Nursing theories have been developed from other disciplines such as psychology, sociology, education and biological sciences. You may wish to understand the importance of a theory. Theory underpins research. It also provides a way of explaining the meaning of research findings, or a language for the communication of nursing knowledge.</p>
<p>Nursing practice can, therefore, be explored and explained through the use of common concepts, for example, pain, grief, stress, quality of care.</p>
<p>Patients and practitioners have to share the findings of research for the knowledge base to grow and to be utilised. From these discussion concepts, models and nursing theories are interlinked and they form the basis of professional nursing practice.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-nursing-council-of-kenya">The Nursing Council of Kenya<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-nursing-council-of-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The Nursing Council of Kenya was established by the Nurses Act, Chapter 257 of the laws of Kenya. The Council is a corporate body having perpetual succession and a common seal with power to sue and be sued and to purchase, hold, manage and dispose of land and other property and to enter into such contracts, as it may consider necessary or expedient.</p>
<p>On the other hand, the Nurses Act, Chapter 257 of the laws of Kenya was enacted as an Act of Parliament to make provision for the training, registration, enrolment and licensing of nurses, to regulate their conduct and to ensure their maximum participation in the health care of the community and for connected purposes (Nurses Act 1985).</p>
<p>The membership of the council consists of:</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Two ex-officials...</th><th>...the Director of Medical Services and the Chief Nursing officer.</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>One person...</td><td>...responsible for education.</td></tr><tr><td>Two persons...</td><td>...representing religious organisations providing health services in Kenya.</td></tr><tr><td>Two persons...</td><td>...representing nursing associations (one from NNAK and one from KEPNA (Kenya Progressive Nurses Association).</td></tr><tr><td>Four persons...</td><td>...nominated by the outgoing council to represent: General Nursing, Midwifery and Community Health Nursing.</td></tr><tr><td>Eleven elected members...</td><td>...who may be involved in clinical practice, nursing education and administration. They must be registered nurses as follows: Three registered nurses, three midwives, three community health nurses and two psychiatric nurses.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The functions of the Nursing Council are carried out through committees, that is, the Full Council and six standing committees</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="functions-of-the-nursing-council">Functions of the Nursing Council<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-the-nursing-council" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The functions of the Nursing Council are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Establishing and improving of all branches of the nursing profession in all their aspects and to safeguard the interest of all nurses</li>
<li>Establishing and improving the standards of professional nursing and of health care within the community</li>
<li>Prescribing and regulating syllabuses of instruction and courses of training for persons seeking registration or enrolment under the Act</li>
<li>Recommending to the Minister institutions to be approved for the training of persons seeking registration or enrolment under the Act</li>
<li>Prescribing and conducting examinations for persons seeking registration or enrolment under the Act.</li>
<li>Prescribing badges, insignia or uniforms to be worn by persons registered, licensed or enrolled under the Act</li>
<li>Regarding the conduct of person registered, licensed or enrolled under the act, and to take such disciplinary measures as may be necessary to</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>maintain a proper standard of conduct among such persons</p>
<ul>
<li>Regarding the standards for nursing care, qualified staff, facilities, conditions and environment of health institutions</li>
<li>Directing and supervising the compilation and maintenance of registers, rolls and records required to be kept under sections 12, 14 and 16</li>
<li>Advising the Minister on matters concerning all aspects of nursing</li>
</ul>
